# Code Context Agent Comparison

## Case
- Name: multi_agent_session_isolation
- Description: Ask how sub-agents share or isolate session state / message history in a multi-agent setup.
- Prompt: In trpc-agent-go's multi-agent system, when a coordinator LLMAgent calls a sub-agent via AgentTool or via WithSubAgents, how is session state isolated between them? Please explain: (1) whether they share the same session by default, (2) what the MessageFilterMode values (FullContext / RequestContext / IsolatedRequest / IsolatedInvocation) mean and when each should be used, (3) how GraphAgent's WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages differs from LLMAgent.WithMessageFilterMode(IsolatedInvocation) especially for multi-turn tool calling, and (4) how skill state keys are scoped between coordinator and sub-agent. Cite exact function / option names and file paths.
- Run Mode: both

## Local Agent + code_search
### Final Answer
```text
Perfect! Now I have comprehensive information. Let me compile the final answer.

In trpc-agent-go's multi-agent system, session state isolation between a coordinator LLMAgent and sub-agents is controlled through multiple mechanisms:

## (1) Session Sharing by Default

**Yes, they share the same session by default.** When a coordinator calls a sub-agent via `AgentTool` or `WithSubAgents`, the sub-agent invocation is created by cloning the parent invocation using `parentInvocation.Clone()` (in `tool/agent/agent_tool.go`, method `callWithParentInvocation`, lines 196-223, and `agent/invocation.go`, method `Clone`, lines 1099-1147). The cloned invocation inherits:
- `Session` (same session object)
- `SessionService` 
- `MemoryService`
- `ArtifactService`

This means both coordinator and sub-agent read from and write to the **same session**, and events from both are persisted under the same `sessionID`.

## (2) MessageFilterMode Values and Usage

Defined in `agent/llmagent/option.go` (lines 101-112) and `agent/graphagent/option.go` (lines 69-80), configured via `llmagent.WithMessageFilterMode()` or `graphagent.WithMessageFilterMode()`:

- **`FullContext`**: Includes all historical messages + current request messages that match via **prefix matching** on `filterKey`. Maps to `BranchFilterModePrefix` + `TimelineFilterAll`. Use when the agent needs full conversation history including ancestor/descendant agent messages.

- **`RequestContext`**: Only messages from the **current request cycle** (one `runner.Run` call) that match via **prefix matching**. Maps to `BranchFilterModePrefix` + `TimelineFilterCurrentRequest`. Use when you want agents to see only current-run context but still include related agent branches.

- **`IsolatedRequest`**: Only messages from the current request cycle with **exact filterKey match**. Maps to `BranchFilterModeExact` + `TimelineFilterCurrentRequest`. Use when the agent should only see its own messages within the current request, ignoring sub-agents and parent.

- **`IsolatedInvocation`**: Only messages from the **current invocation** (single agent call) with **exact match**. Maps to `BranchFilterModeExact` + `TimelineFilterCurrentInvocation`. Use for the strictest isolation where the agent only sees messages from its own single invocation cycle.

## (3) WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages vs WithMessageFilterMode(IsolatedInvocation)

**`graph.WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages(true)`** (in `graph/state_graph.go`, lines 440-449):
- Sets `include_contents="none"` in the child agent's runtime state
- **Completely blocks session history injection** at the message-loading stage
- The sub-agent **cannot see tool results** from its own prior turns
- **Breaks multi-turn tool calling** because the agent never sees `role=tool` messages
- Use only for **single-turn black-box sub-agents** that don't use tools

**`llmagent.WithMessageFilterMode(IsolatedInvocation)`** (in `agent/llmagent/option.go`, lines 1325-1345):
- Filters messages via `BranchFilterModeExact` + `TimelineFilterCurrentInvocation`
- The agent **can still see its own tool results** within the same invocation
- **Supports multi-turn tool calling** because tool messages are preserved within the invocation scope
- Use when a sub-agent needs tools and must continue after tool execution

**Key difference**: `WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages(true)` is a hard cutoff that prevents all session history loading (breaking tool multi-turn), while `IsolatedInvocation` allows the agent to see its own invocation's messages (preserving tool multi-turn).

## (4) Skill State Key Scoping

Skill state keys are **scoped by agent name** to prevent cross-contamination in multi-agent runs sharing the same Session. Defined in `skill/repository.go` (lines 461-469):

- **`StateKeyLoadedByAgentPrefix`** (constant: `"temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:"`): Scopes which skills are marked as "loaded" per agent. When a sub-agent calls `skill_load`, the key becomes `"temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:<agentName>:<skillName>"`, preventing the coordinator from seeing the sub-agent's loaded skill bodies in its own prompt.

- **`StateKeyLoadedOrderByAgentPrefix`** (constant: `"temp:skill:loaded_order_by_agent:"`): Scopes the skill touch-order (for `MaxLoadedSkills` cap) per agent, so each agent maintains its own recent-skill window.

This ensures that when a coordinator and sub-agent share the same Session (default behavior), a sub-agent's `skill_load` **does not** inflate the coordinator's prompt with unrelated skill content (see `examples/skillisolation/README.md`).
```

This retry only applies when AddSessionSummary is enabled.\\n\\tContextCompactionThresholdRatio float64\\n\\t// ContextCompactionToolResultMaxTokens sets the token threshold above\\n\\t// which\\n\\t// historical tool results are replaced with a placeholder.\\n\\tContextCompactionToolResultMaxTokens int\\n\\t// ContextCompactionKeepRecentRequests preserves the latest N completed\\n\\t// requests in full when request-side context compaction is enabled.\\n\\tContextCompactionKeepRecentRequests int\\n\\t// ContextCompactionOversizedToolResultMaxTokens sets the token threshold\\n\\t// above which any tool result (including from the current request) is\\n\\t// truncated using head+tail preservation. This fires regardless of\\n\\t// EnableContextCompaction. 0 disables it.\\n\\tContextCompactionOversizedToolResultMaxTokens int\\n\\t// summaryFormatter allows custom formatting of session summary content.\\n\\t// When nil (default), uses the default formatSummaryContent function.\\n\\tsummaryFormatter func(summary string) string\\n\\n\\t// MaxLLMCalls is an optional upper bound on the number of LLM calls\\n\\t// allowed per invocation for this agent. ## Augment Agent + MCP
### Final Answer
```text
Based on the code search results, I now have comprehensive information to answer the user's question about session state isolation in trpc-agent-go's multi-agent system.

## Answer

In trpc-agent-go's multi-agent system, session state isolation between coordinators and sub-agents works as follows:

### (1) Session Sharing by Default

**They share the same session by default.** When a coordinator calls a sub-agent via `AgentTool` or via `WithSubAgents`:

- **AgentTool** (in `tool/agent/agent_tool.go`): The `callWithParentInvocation` method at line 199 explicitly reuses the parent's session: `subInv := parentInv.Clone(...)` creates a child invocation that shares `parentInv.Session`. The comment at line 186 confirms: *"Prefer to reuse parent invocation + session so the child can see parent history according to the configured history scope."*

- **WithSubAgents** in GraphAgent: Sub-agents inherit the parent's session through invocation context propagation during graph execution.

This shared session means events written by both coordinator and sub-agent are stored in the same `session.Events` list, enabling message history visibility based on filtering rules.

---

### (2) MessageFilterMode Values

Defined in `agent/llmagent/option.go` (lines 100-111) and `agent/graphagent/option.go` (lines 68-80):

- **`FullContext`**: `TimelineFilterAll + BranchFilterModePrefix`  
  Includes **all historical messages** where the `FilterKey` matches by prefix. Use when an agent needs complete conversation history including past requests and sibling agent interactions.

- **`RequestContext`**: `TimelineFilterCurrentRequest + BranchFilterModePrefix`  
  Includes only messages from the **current request cycle** (current `runner.Run` call) with prefix matching. Filters out previous historical records but keeps all messages related to this request. Use for stateless request-response workflows.

- **`IsolatedRequest`**: `TimelineFilterCurrentRequest + BranchFilterModeExact`  
  Includes only messages from the current request cycle where `FilterKey` **exactly matches** the agent's key. Use when an agent should only see its own messages within the current request, not sibling agents.

- **`IsolatedInvocation`**: `TimelineFilterCurrentInvocation + BranchFilterModeExact`  
  Includes only messages from the **current invocation** (one execution chain of the agent) with exact `FilterKey` match. Use for strict isolation where each agent invocation only sees messages it generated in that specific run. Critical for multi-turn tool calling in sub-agents (see next section).

Implementation in `internal/flow/processor/content.go`:
- `TimelineFilterAll` (line 51): includes all historical records
- `TimelineFilterCurrentRequest` (line 54): filters by `evt.RequestID == inv.RunOptions.RequestID`
- `TimelineFilterCurrentInvocation` (line 57): filters by `evt.InvocationID == inv.InvocationID`
- `BranchFilterModePrefix` (line 62): `evt.Filter(filterKey)` prefix match
- `BranchFilterModeExact` (line 73): `evt.FilterKey == filterKey` exact match

---

### (3) WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages vs IsolatedInvocation for Multi-Turn Tool Calling

**GraphAgent's `WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages(true)`** (in `graph/state_graph.go`, lines 440-449):

Sets `CfgKeyIncludeContents = "none"` in the child's runtime state (line 2544 in `state_graph.go`). This **completely prevents** the child from reading session history when building model requests. The child becomes a "black box" seeing only its current input.

**Problem for multi-turn tool calling:** When the child agent calls a tool, the framework executes it and adds a `role=tool` message to the session. On the next model request, the child needs to see this tool result to continue reasoning. But with `include_contents=none`, the child **cannot see its own tool results** (documented in `docs/mkdocs/en/graph.md`, lines 1343-1362). Symptoms: the agent repeats the first tool call in an infinite loop.

**Solution:** Use `llmagent.WithMessageFilterMode(llmagent.IsolatedInvocation)` instead (documented in `docs/mkdocs/zh/graph.md`, lines 1427-1432):

- **Preserves session seeding** so tool results are visible
- **Filters message history** to only the current invocation using `TimelineFilterCurrentInvocation + BranchFilterModeExact`
- The child sees its own tool call → tool result → continue loop, but remains isolated from parent/sibling history

The `getCurrentInvocationMessages` function in `internal/flow/processor/content.go` (lines 1276-1288) specifically handles this: when `include_contents=none`, it still fetches messages from `evt.InvocationID == inv.InvocationID` to preserve the ReAct loop context (comment at lines 597-600).

**Key difference:** 
- `WithSubgraphIsolatedMessages(true)`: Absolute message isolation via runtime config
- `IsolatedInvocation`: Selective filtering that preserves tool call history within the same invocation

---

### (4) Skill State Key Scoping

Skill state keys are **scoped by agent name** to prevent cross-agent pollution (introduced in `skill/repository.go`, lines 461-468):

- **Legacy keys** (unscoped): `temp:skill:loaded:{skillName}`, `temp:skill:docs:{skillName}`
- **Scoped keys**: `temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:{agentName}/{skillName}`, `temp:skill:docs_by_agent:{agentName}/{skillName}`

Implementation in `skill/state_keys.go`:
- `LoadedKey(agentName, skillName)` (lines 27-40): Returns `"temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:{agentName}/{skillName}"` when `agentName` is non-empty, otherwise falls back to legacy key
- `DocsKey(agentName, skillName)` (lines 42-55): Same scoping pattern for doc selections
- `LoadedOrderKey(agentName)` (in `skill/state_order.go`, lines 18-30): Scopes skill touch order per agent

When a sub-agent calls `skill_load`, the `LoadTool.StateDeltaForInvocation` method (in `tool/skill/load.go`, lines 150-171) uses `inv.AgentName` to generate scoped keys (line 162). This ensures:
- Sub-agent's `skill_load` writes to `temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:child/{skillName}`
- Coordinator only sees skills under `temp:skill:loaded_by_agent:coordinator/{skillName}`
- No cross-contamination of loaded skill bodies/docs in prompts

Example: `examples/skillisolation/README.md` documents this behavior (lines 7-14): *"A coordinator agent calls a sub-agent (via AgentTool). The sub-agent calls skill_load. trpc-agent-go now scopes skill state keys by agent name, so a sub-agent's skill_load does not automatically inflate the coordinator's prompt."*
```

[

    "text": "{\"branch\":\"main\",\"repo_name\":\"trpc-agent-go\",\"repo_owner\":\"trpc-group\",\"results\":\"The following code sections were retrieved:\\nPath: agent/invocation.go\\n...\\n   668\\t\\n   669\\t// WithToolFilter sets a custom tool filter function for this specific run.\\n   670\\t// The filter function receives a context and a tool, and returns true if the tool should be included.\\n   671\\t//\\n   672\\t// This is useful for:\\n   673\\t//   - Permission control: restrict tool access based on user roles or runtime conditions\\n   674\\t//   - Cost optimization: reduce token usage by limiting tool descriptions\\n   675\\t//   - Feature isolation: limit capabilities for specific use cases\\n   676\\t//   - Dynamic filtering: filter tools based on runtime state, session data, etc.\\n   677\\t//\\n   678\\t// Example - Simple name-based filtering:\\n   679\\t//\\n   680\\t//\\trunner.Run(ctx, userID, sessionID, message,\\n   681\\t//\\t    agent.WithToolFilter(tool.NewIncludeToolNamesFilter(\\\"calculator\\\", \\\"time_tool\\\")),\\n   682\\t//\\t)\\n   683\\t//\\n   684\\t// Example - WithToolFilter controls which tools are visible to the model.\\n   718\\t//   - WithToolExecutionFilter controls which tool calls are auto-executed\\n   719\\t//     after the model requests them.\\n   720\\t//\\n   721\\t// When the filter returns false for a tool, the tool call is not executed\\n   722\\t// and the run ends after emitting the assistant tool_call response. The\\n   723\\t// caller can then execute the tool externally and provide a RoleTool\\n   724\\t// message with the tool result to continue.\\n   725\\tfunc WithToolExecutionFilter(filter tool.FilterFunc) RunOption {\\n   726\\t\\treturn func(opts *RunOptions) {\\n   727\\t\\t\\topts.ToolExecutionFilter = filter\\n   728\\t\\t}\\n   729\\t}\\n...\\n   991\\t\\n   992\\t\\t// ToolFilter is a custom function to filter tools for this run.\\n   993\\t\\t// If set, only tools for which the filter returns true will be available to the model.\\n   994\\t\\t// If nil, all registered tools will be available (default behavior).\\n   995\\t\\t//\\n   996\\t\\t// The filter function receives:\\n   997\\t\\t//   -
